skipped.\\n113: \\tSkip\\n114: \\t// Pending means that the scheduling process is finished successfully,\\n115: \\t// but the plugin wants to stop the scheduling cycle/binding cycle here.\\n116: \\t//\\n117: \\t// For example, the DRA plugin sometimes needs to wait for the external device driver\\n118: \\t// to provision the resource for the Pod.\\n119: \\t// It's different from when to component to do something based on that scheduling result.\\n122: \\t//\\n123: \\t// We regard the backoff as a penalty of wasting the scheduling cycle.\\n124: \\t// In the case of returning Pending, All PreFilter\\n400: \\t// plugins must return success or the pod will be rejected. PreFilter could optionally\\n401: \\t// return a PreFilterResult to influence which nodes to evaluate downstream. This is useful\\n402: \\t// for cases where it is possible to determine the subset of nodes to process in O(1) time.\\n403: \\t// When PreFilterResult filters out some Nodes, the framework considers Nodes that are filtered out as getting \\\"UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\\\".\\n404: \\t// i.e., those Nodes will be out of the candidates of the preemption.\\n405: \\t//\\n406: \\t// When it returns Skip status, returned PreFilterResult and other fields in status are just ignored,\\n407: \\t// and coupled Filter plugin/PreFilterExtensions() will be skipped in this scheduling cycle.\\n408: \\tPreFilter(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod) (*PreFilterResult, *Status)\\n409: \\t// PreFilterExtensions returns a PreFilterExtensions interface if the plugin implements one,\\n410: \\t// or nil if it does not. The framework guarantees that the extensions\\n412: \\t// AddPod/RemovePod will only be called after PreFilter, possibly on a cloned\\n413: \\t// CycleState, and may call those functions more than once before calling\\n414: \\t// Filter again on a specific node.\\n415: \\tPreFilterExtensions() PreFilterExtensions\\n416: }\\n417: \\n418: // FilterPlugin is an interface for Filter plugins. These plugins are called at the\\n419: // filter extension point for filtering out hosts that cannot run a pod.\\n420: // This concept used to be called 'predicate' in the original scheduler.\\n421: // These plugins should return \\\"Success\\\", \\\"Unschedulable\\\" or \\\"Error\\\" in Status.code.\\n422: // However, the scheduler accepts other valid codes as well.\\n423: // Anything other than \\\"Success\\\" will lead to exclusion of the given host from\\n424: // running the pod.\\n425: type FilterPlugin interface {\\n426: \\tPlugin\\n427: \\t// Filter is called by the scheduling framework.\\n428: \\t// All FilterPlugins should return \\\"Success\\\" to declare that\\n429: \\t// the given node fits the pod. If Filter doesn't return \\\"Success\\\",\\n430: \\t// it will return \\\"Unschedulable\\\", \\\"UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\\\" or \\\"Error\\\".\\n431: \\t// For the node being evaluated, Filter plugins should look at the passed\\n432: \\t// nodeInfo reference for this particular node's information (e.g., pods\\n433: \\t// considered to be running on the node) instead of looking it up in the\\n434: \\t// NodeInfoSnapshot because we don't guarantee that they will be the same.\\n435: \\t// For example, during preemption, we may pass a copy of the original\\n436: \\t// nodeInfo object that has some pods removed from it to evaluate the\\n437: \\t// possibility of preempting them to schedule the target pod.\\n438: \\tFilter(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, nodeInfo *NodeInfo) *Status\\n439: }\\n440: \\n441: // PostFilterPlugin is an interface for \\\"PostFilter\\\" plugins. These plugins are called\\n442: // after a pod cannot be scheduled.\\n443: type PostFilterPlugin interface {\\n444: \\tPlugin\\n445: \\t// PostFilter is called by the scheduling framework\\n446: \\t// when the scheduling cycle failed at PreFilter or Filter by Unschedulable or UnschedulableAndUnresolvable.\\n447: \\t// NodeToStatusMap has statuses that each Node got in the Filter phase.\\n448: \\t// If this scheduling cycle failed at PreFilter, all Nodes have the status from the rejector PreFilter plugin in NodeToStatusMap.\\n449: \\t// Note that the scheduling framework runs PostFilter plugins even when PreFilter returned UnschedulableAndUnresolvable.\\n450: \\t// In that case, NodeToStatusMap contains all Nodes with UnschedulableAndUnresolvable.\\n451: \\t//\\n452: \\t// Also, ignoring Nodes with UnschedulableAndUnresolvable is the responsibility of each PostFilter plugin,\\n453: \\t// meaning NodeToStatusMap obviously could have Nodes with UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\\n454: \\t// and the scheduling framework does call PostFilter even when all Nodes in NodeToStatusMap are UnschedulableAndUnresolvable.\\n455: \\t//\\n456: \\t// A PostFilter plugin should return one of the following statuses:\\n457: \\t// - Unschedulable: the plugin gets executed successfully but the pod cannot be made schedulable.\\n458: \\t// - Success: the plugin gets executed successfully and the pod can be made schedulable.\\n459: \\t// - Error: the plugin aborts due to some internal error.\\n460: \\t//\\n461: \\t// Informational plugins should be configured ahead of other ones, and always return Unschedulable status.\\n462: \\t// Optionally, a non-nil PostFilterResult may be returned along with a Success status. For example,\\n463: \\t// a preemption plugin may choose to return nominatedNodeName, so that framework can reuse that to update the\\n464: \\t// preemptor pod's .spec.status.nominatedNodeName field.\\n465: \\tPostFilter(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, filteredNodeStatusMap NodeToStatusMap) (*PostFilterResult, *Status)\\n466: }\\n467: \\n468: // PreScorePlugin is an interface for \\\"PreScore\\\" plugin. PreScore is an\\n469: // informational extension point. Plugins will be called with a list of nodes\\n470: // that passed the filtering phase. A plugin may use this data to update internal\\n471: // state or to generate logs/metrics.\\n472: type PreScorePlugin interface {\\n473: \\tPlugin\\n474: \\t// PreScore is called by the scheduling framework after a list of nodes\\n475: \\t// passed the filtering phase. All prescore plugins must return success or\\n476: \\t// the pod will be rejected\\n477: \\t// When it returns Skip status, other fields in status are just ignored,\\n478: \\t// and coupled Score plugin will be skipped in this scheduling cycle.\\n479: \\tPreScore(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, nodes []*NodeInfo) *Status\\n480: }\\n481: \\n482: // ScoreExtensions is an interface for Score extended functionality.\\n483: type ScoreExtensions interface {\\n484: \\t// NormalizeScore is called for all node scores produced by the same plugin's \\\"Score\\\"\\n485: \\t// method. A successful run of NormalizeScore will update the scores list and return\\n486: \\t// a success status.\\n487: \\tNormalizeScore(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod, scores NodeScoreList) *Status\\n488: }\\n489: \\n490: // ScorePlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \\\"Score\\\" plugins to rank\\n491: // nodes that passed the filtering phase.\\n492: type ScorePlugin interface {\\n493: \\tPlugin\\n494: \\t// Score is called on each filtered node. It must return success and an integer\\n495: \\t// indicating the rank of the node. All scoring plugins must return success or\\n496: \\t// the pod will be rejected.\\n497: \\tScore(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string) (int64, *Status)\\n498: \\n499: \\t// ScoreExtensions returns a ScoreExtensions interface if it implements one, or nil if does not.\\n500: \\tScoreExtensions() ScoreExtensions\\n501: }\\n502: \\n503: // ReservePlugin is an interface for plugins with Reserve and Unreserve\\n504: // methods. These are meant to update the state of the plugin. This concept\\n505: // used to be called 'assume' in the original scheduler. These plugins should\\n506: // return only Success or Error in Status.code. However, the scheduler accepts\\n507: // other valid codes as well. Anything other than Success will lead to\\n508: // rejection of the pod.\\n509: type ReservePlugin interface {\\n510: \\tPlugin\\n511: \\t// Reserve is called by the scheduling framework when the scheduler cache is\\n512: \\t// updated. If this method returns a failed Status, the scheduler will call\\n513: \\t// the Unreserve method for all enabled ReservePlugins.\\n514: \\tReserve(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string) *Status\\n515: \\t// Unreserve is called by the scheduling framework when a reserved pod was\\n516: \\t// rejected, an error occurred during reservation of subsequent plugins, or\\n517: \\t// in a later phase. The Unreserve method implementation must be idempotent\\n518: \\t// and may be called by the scheduler even if the corresponding Reserve\\n519: \\t// method for the same plugin was not called.\\n520: \\tUnreserve(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string)\\n521: }\\n522: \\n523: // PreBindPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \\\"PreBind\\\" plugins.\\n524: // These plugins are called before a pod being scheduled.\\n525: type PreBindPlugin interface {\\n526: \\tPlugin\\n527: \\t// PreBind is called before binding a pod. All prebind plugins must return\\n528: \\t// success or the pod will be rejected and won't be sent for binding.\\n529: \\tPreBind(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string) *Status\\n530: }\\n531: \\n532: // PostBindPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \\\"PostBind\\\" plugins.\\n533: // These plugins are called after a pod is successfully bound to a node.\\n534: type PostBindPlugin interface {\\n535: \\tPlugin\\n536: \\t// PostBind is called after a pod is successfully bound. These plugins are\\n537: \\t// informational. A common application of this extension point is for cleaning\\n538: \\t// up. If a plugin needs to clean-up its state after a pod is scheduled and\\n539: \\t// bound, PostBind is the extension point that it should register.\\n540: \\tPostBind(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string)\\n541: }\\n542: \\n543: // PermitPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \\\"Permit\\\" plugins.\\n544: // These plugins are called before a pod is bound to a node.\\n545: type PermitPlugin interface {\\n546: \\tPlugin\\n547: \\t// Permit is called before binding a pod (and before prebind plugins). Permit\\n548: \\t// plugins are used to prevent or delay the binding of a Pod. A permit plugin\\n549: \\t// must return success or wait with timeout duration, or the pod will be rejected.\\n550: \\t// The pod will also be rejected if the wait timeout or the pod is rejected while\\n551: \\t// waiting. Note that if the plugin returns \\\"wait\\\", the framework will wait only\\n552: \\t// after running the remaining plugins given that no other plugin rejects the pod.\\n553: \\tPermit(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string) (*Status, time.Duration)\\n554: }\\n555: \\n556: // BindPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \\\"Bind\\\" plugins. Bind\\n557: // plugins are used to bind a pod to a Node.\\n558: type BindPlugin interface {\\n559: \\tPlugin\\n560: \\t// Bind plugins will not be called until all pre-bind plugins have completed. Each\\n561: \\t// bind plugin is called in the configured order. A bind plugin may choose whether\\n562: \\t// or not to handle the given Pod. If a bind plugin chooses to handle a Pod, the\\n563: \\t// remaining bind plugins are skipped. When a bind plugin does not handle a pod,\\n564: \\t// it must return Skip in its Status code. If a bind plugin returns an Error, the\\n565: \\t// pod is rejected and will not be bound.\\n566: \\tBind(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string) *Status\\n567: }\\n568: \\n569: // Framework manages the set of plugins in use by the scheduling framework.\\n570: // Configured plugins are called at specified points in a scheduling context.\\n571: type Framework interface {\\n572: \\tHandle\\n573: \\n574: \\t// PreEnqueuePlugins returns the registered preEnqueue plugins.\\n575: \\tPreEnqueuePlugins() []PreEnqueuePlugin\\n576: \\n577: \\t// EnqueueExtensions returns the registered Enqueue extensions.\\n578: \\tEnqueueExtensions() []EnqueueExtensions\\n579: \\n580: \\t// QueueSortFunc returns the function to sort pods in scheduling queue\\n581: \\tQueueSortFunc() LessFunc\\n582: \\n583: \\t// RunPreFilterPlugins runs the set of configured PreFilter plugins. It returns\\n584: \\t// *Status and its code is set to non-success if any of the plugins returns\\n585: \\t// anything but Success. If a non-success status is returned, then the scheduling\\n586: \\t// cycle is aborted.\\n587: \\t// It also returns a PreFilterResult, which may influence what or how many nodes to\\n588: \\t// evaluate downstream.\\n589: \\tRunPreFilterPlugins(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, pod *v1.Pod) (*PreFilterResult, *Status)\\n590: \\n591: \\t// RunPostFilterPlugins runs the set of configured PostFilter plugins.\\n592: \\t// PostFilter plugins can either be informational, in which case should be configured\\n593: \\t// to execute first and return Unschedulable status, or ones that try to change the\\n594: \\t// cluster state to make the pod potentially schedulable in a future scheduling cycle.\\n595: \\tRunPostFilterPlugins(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, filteredNodeStatusMap NodeToStatusMap) (*PostFilterResult, *Status)\\n596: \\n597: \\t// RunPreBindPlugins runs the set of configured PreBind plugins. In either case the pod is not going to be bound.\\n602: \\tRunPreBindPlugins(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, nodeName string) *Status\\n603: \\n604: \\t// RunPostBindPlugins runs the set of configured PostBind plugins.\\n605: \\tRunPostBindPlugins(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, nodeName string)\\n606: \\n607: \\t// RunReservePluginsReserve runs the Reserve method of the set of\\n608: \\t// configured Reserve plugins. In\\n610: \\t// such case, pod will not be scheduled.\\n611: \\tRunReservePluginsReserve(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, nodeName string) *Status\\n612: \\n613: \\t// RunReservePluginsUnreserve runs the Unreserve method of the set of\\n614: \\t// configured Reserve plugins.\\n615: \\tRunReservePluginsUnreserve(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, nodeName string)\\n616: \\n617: \\t// RunPermitPlugins runs the set of configured Permit plugins. A Bind plugin may choose\\n629: \\t// whether or not to handle the given Pod. If a Bind plugin chooses to skip the\\n630: \\t// binding, it should return code=5(\\\"skip\\\") status. It is\\n661: // passed to the plugin factories at the time of plugin initialization. Plugins\\n662: // must store and use this handle to call framework functions.\\n663: type Handle interface {\\n664: \\t// PodNominator abstracts operations to maintain nominated Pods.\\n665: \\tPodNominator\\n666: \\t// PluginsRunner abstracts operations to run some plugins.\\n667: \\tPluginsRunner\\n668: \\t// SnapshotSharedLister returns listers from the latest NodeInfo Snapshot. plugins.\\n73: type Code int\\n74: \\n75: // These are predefined codes used in a Status.\\n76: // Note: when you add a new status, you have to add it in `codes` slice below.\\n77: const (\\n78: \\t// Success means that plugin ran correctly and found pod schedulable.\\n79: \\t// NOTE: A nil status is also considered as \\\"Success\\\".\\n80: \\tSuccess Code = iota\\n81: \\t// Error is one of the failures, used for internal plugin errors, unexpected input, etc.\\n82: \\t// Plugin shouldn't return this code for expected failures, like Unschedulable.\\n83: \\t// Since it's the unexpected failure, the scheduling queue registers the pod without unschedulable plugins.\\n84: \\t// Meaning, the Pod will be requeued to activeQ/backoffQ soon.\\n85: \\tError\\n86: \\t// Unschedulable is one of the failures, used when a plugin finds a pod unschedulable.\\n87: \\t// If it's returned from PreFilter or Filter, the scheduler might attempt to\\n88: \\t// run other postFilter plugins like preemption to get this pod scheduled.\\n89: \\t// Use UnschedulableAndUnresolvable to make the scheduler skipping other postFilter plugins.\\n90: \\t// The accompanying status message should explain why the pod is unschedulable.\\n91: \\t//\\n92: \\t// We regard the backoff as a penalty of wasting the scheduling cycle.\\n93: \\t// When the scheduling queue requeues Pods, which was rejected with Unschedulable in the last scheduling,\\n94: \\t// the Pod goes through backoff.\\n95: \\tUnschedulable\\n96: \\t// UnschedulableAndUnresolvable is used when a plugin finds a pod unschedulable and\\n97: \\t// other postFilter plugins like preemption would not change anything.\\n98: \\t// See the comment on PostFilter interface for more details about how PostFilter should handle this status.\\n99: \\t// Plugins should return Unschedulable if it is possible that the pod can get scheduled\\n100: \\t// after running other postFilter plugins.\\n101: \\t// The accompanying status message should explain why the pod is unschedulable.\\n102: \\t//\\n103: \\t// We regard the backoff as a penalty of wasting the scheduling cycle.\\n104: \\t// When the scheduling queue requeues Pods, which was rejected with UnschedulableAndUnresolvable in the last scheduling,\\n105: \\t// the Pod goes through backoff.\\n106: \\tUnschedulableAndUnresolvable\\n107: \\t// Wait is used when a Permit plugin finds a pod scheduling should wait.\\n108: \\tWait\\n109: \\t// Skip is used in the following scenarios:\\n110: \\t// - when a Bind plugin chooses to skip binding.\\n111: \\t// - when a PreFilter plugin returns Skip so that coupled Filter plugin/PreFilterExtensions() will be skipped.\\n112: \\t// - when a PreScore plugin returns Skip so that coupled Score plugin will be skipped.\\n113: \\tSkip\\n114: \\t// Pending means that the scheduling process is finished successfully,\\n115: \\t// but the plugin wants to stop the scheduling cycle/binding cycle here.\\n116: \\t//\\n117: \\t// For example, the DRA plugin sometimes needs to wait for the external device driver\\n118: \\t// to provision the resource for the Pod.\\n119: \\t// It's different from when to return Unschedulable/UnschedulableAndUnresolvable,\\n120: \\t// because in this case, the scheduler decides where the Pod can go successfully,\\n121: \\t// but we need to wait for the external component to do something based on that scheduling result.\\n122: \\t//\\n123: \\t// We regard the backoff as a penalty of wasting the scheduling cycle.\\n124: \\t// In the case of returning Pending, we cannot say the scheduling cycle is wasted\\n125: \\t// because the scheduling result is used to proceed the Pod's scheduling forward,\\n126: \\t// that particular scheduling cycle is failed though.\\n127: \\t// So, Pods rejected by such reasons don't need to suffer a penalty (backoff).\\n128: \\t// When the scheduling queue requeues Pods, which was rejected with Pending in the last scheduling,\\n129: \\t// the Pod goes to activeQ directly ignoring backoff.\\n130: \\tPending\\n131: )\\n132: \\n133: // This list should be exactly the same as the codes iota defined above in the same order.\\n134: var codes = []string{\\\"Success\\\", \\\"Error\\\", \\\"Unschedulable\\\", \\\"UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\\\", \\\"Wait\\\", \\\"Skip\\\", \\\"Pending\\\"}\\n135: \\n136: func (c Code) String() string {\\n137: \\treturn codes[c]\\n138: }\\n139: \\n140: const (\\n141: \\t// MaxNodeScore is the maximum score a Score plugin is expected to return.\\n142: \\tMaxNodeScore int64 = 100\\n143: \\n144: \\t// MinNodeScore is the minimum score a Score plugin is expected to return.\\n145: \\tMinNodeScore int64 = 0\\n146: \\n147: \\t// MaxTotalScore is the maximum total score.\\n148: \\tMaxTotalScore int64 = math.MaxInt64\\n149: )\\n150: \\n151: // PodsToActivateKey is a reserved state key for stashing pods.\\n152: // If the stashed pods are present in unschedulablePods or }\\n214: \\n215: // WithPlugin sets the given plugin name to s.plugin,\\n216: // and returns the given status object.\\n217: func (s *Status) WithPlugin(plugin string) *Status {\\n218: }\\n272: \\n273: // Equal checks equality of two statuses. Each\\n561: \\t// bind plugin is called in the configured order. A bind plugin may choose whether\\n562: \\t// or not to handle the given Pod. If a bind plugin chooses to handle a Pod, the\\n563: \\t// remaining bind plugins are skipped. When a bind plugin does not handle a pod,\\n564: \\t// it must return Skip in its Status code. If a bind plugin returns an Error, the\\n565: \\t// pod is rejected and will not be bound.\\n566: \\tBind(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string) *Status\\n567: }\\n568: \\n569: // Framework manages the set of plugins in use by the scheduling framework.\\n570: // Configured plugins are called at specified points in a scheduling context.\\n571: type Framework interface {\\n572: \\tHandle\\n573: \\n574: \\t// PreEnqueuePlugins returns the registered preEnqueue plugins.\\n575: \\tPreEnqueuePlugins() []PreEnqueuePlugin\\n576: \\n577: \\t// EnqueueExtensions returns the registered Enqueue extensions.\\n578: \\tEnqueueExtensions() []EnqueueExtensions\\n579: \\n580: \\t// QueueSortFunc returns the function to sort pods in scheduling queue\\n581: \\tQueueSortFunc() LessFunc\\n582: \\n583: \\t// RunPreFilterPlugins runs the set of configured PreFilter plugins. If a non-success status is returned, then the scheduling\\n586: \\t// cycle is aborted.\\n587: \\t// It also returns a PreFilterResult, which may influence what or how many nodes to\\n588: \\t// evaluate downstream.\\n589: \\tRunPreFilterPlugins(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, pod *v1.Pod) (*PreFilterResult, *Status)\\n590: \\n591: \\t// RunPostFilterPlugins runs the set of configured PostFilter plugins.\\n592: \\t// PostFilter plugins can either be informational, in which case should be configured\\n593: \\t// to execute first and return Unschedulable status, or ones that try to change the\\n594: \\t// cluster state to make the pod potentially schedulable in a future scheduling cycle.\\n595: \\tRunPostFilterPlugins(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, filteredNodeStatusMap NodeToStatusMap) (*PostFilterResult, *Status)\\n596: \\n597: \\t// RunPreBindPlugins runs the set of configured PreBind plugins. In\\n610: \\t// such case, pod will not be scheduled.\\n611: \\tRunReservePluginsReserve(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, nodeName string) *Status\\n612: \\n613: \\t// RunReservePluginsUnreserve runs the Unreserve method of the set of\\n614: \\t// configured Reserve plugins.\\n615: \\tRunReservePluginsUnreserve(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, nodeName string)\\n616: \\n617: \\t// RunPermitPlugins runs the set of configured Permit plugins. Plugins\\n662: // must store and use this handle to call framework functions.\\n663: type Handle interface {\\n664: \\t// PodNominator abstracts operations to maintain nominated Pods.\\n665: \\tPodNominator\\n666: \\t// PluginsRunner abstracts operations to run some plugins.\\n667: \\tPluginsRunner\\n668: \\t// SnapshotSharedLister returns listers from the latest NodeInfo Snapshot. \t\"k8s.io/kubernetes/pkg/scheduler/framework/parallelize\"\n41: )\n42: \n43: // NodeScoreList declares a list of nodes and their scores.\n44: type NodeScoreList []NodeScore\n45: \n46: // NodeScore is a struct with node name and score.\n47: type NodeScore struct {\n48: \tName  string\n49: \tScore int64\n50: }\n51: \n52: // NodeToStatusMap declares map from node name to its status.\n53: type NodeToStatusMap map[string]*Status\n54: \n55: // NodePluginScores is a struct with node name and scores for that node.\n56: type NodePluginScores struct {\n57: \t// Name is node name.\n58: \tName string\n59: \t// Scores is scores from plugins and extenders.\n60: \tScores []PluginScore\n61: \t// TotalScore is the total score in Scores.\n62: \tTotalScore int64\n63: }\n64: \n65: // PluginScore is a struct with plugin/extender name and score.\n66: type PluginScore struct {\n67: \t// Name is the name of plugin or extender.\n68: \tName  string\n69: \tScore int64\n70: }\n71: \n72: // Code is the Status code/type which is returned from plugins.\n73: type Code int\n74: \n75: // These are predefined codes used in a Status.\n76: // Note: when you add a new status, you have to add it in `codes` slice below.\n77: const (\n78: \t// Success means that plugin ran correctly and found pod schedulable.\n79: \t// NOTE: A nil status is also considered as \"Success\".\n80: \tSuccess Code = iota\n81: \t// Error is one of the failures, used for internal plugin errors, unexpected input, etc.\n82: \t// Plugin shouldn't return this code for expected failures, like Unschedulable.\n83: \t// Since it's the unexpected failure, the scheduling queue registers the pod without unschedulable plugins.\n84: \t// Meaning, the Pod will be requeued to activeQ/backoffQ soon.\n85: \tError\n86: \t// Unschedulable is one of the failures, used when a plugin finds a pod unschedulable.\n87: \t// If it's returned from PreFilter or Filter, the scheduler might attempt to\n88: \t// run other postFilter plugins like preemption to get this pod scheduled.\n89: \t// Use UnschedulableAndUnresolvable to make the scheduler skipping other postFilter plugins.\n90: \t// The accompanying status message should explain why the pod is unschedulable.\n91: \t//\n92: \t// We regard the backoff as a penalty of wasting the scheduling cycle.\n93: \t// When the scheduling queue requeues Pods, which was rejected with Unschedulable in the last scheduling,\n94: \t// the Pod goes through backoff.\n95: \tUnschedulable\n96: \t// UnschedulableAndUnresolvable is used when a plugin finds a pod unschedulable and\n97: \t// other postFilter plugins like preemption would not change anything.\n98: \t// See the comment on PostFilter interface for more details about how PostFilter should handle this status.\n99: \t// Plugins should return Unschedulable if it is possible that the pod can get scheduled\n100: \t// after running other postFilter plugins.\n101: \t// The accompanying status message should explain why the pod is unschedulable.\n102: \t//\n103: \t// We regard the backoff as a penalty of wasting the scheduling cycle.\n104: \t// When the scheduling queue requeues Pods, which was rejected with UnschedulableAndUnresolvable in the last scheduling,\n105: \t// the Pod goes through backoff.\n106: \tUnschedulableAndUnresolvable\n107: \t// Wait is used when a Permit plugin finds a pod scheduling should wait.\n108: \tWait\n109: \t// Skip is used in the following scenarios:\n110: \t// - when a Bind plugin chooses to skip binding.\n111: \t// - when a PreFilter plugin returns Skip so that coupled Filter plugin/PreFilterExtensions() will be skipped.\n112: \t// - when a PreScore plugin returns Skip so that coupled Score plugin will be skipped.\n113: \tSkip\n114: \t// Pending means that the scheduling process is finished successfully,\n115: \t// but the plugin wants to stop the scheduling cycle/binding cycle here.\n116: \t//\n117: \t// For example, the DRA plugin sometimes needs to wait for the external device driver\n118: \t// to provision the resource for the Pod.\n119: \t// It's different from when to return Unschedulable/UnschedulableAndUnresolvable,\n120: \t// because in this case, the scheduler decides where the Pod can go successfully,\n121: \t// but we need to wait for the external component to do something based on that scheduling result.\n122: \t//\n123: \t// We regard the backoff as a penalty of wasting the scheduling cycle.\n124: \t// In the case of returning Pending, we cannot say the scheduling cycle is wasted\n125: \t// because the scheduling result is used to proceed the Pod's scheduling forward,\n126: \t// that particular scheduling cycle is failed though.\n127: \t// So, Pods rejected by such reasons don't need to suffer a penalty (backoff).\n128: \t// When the scheduling queue requeues Pods, which was rejected with Pending in the last scheduling,\n129: \t// the Pod goes to activeQ directly ignoring backoff.\n130: \tPending\n131: )\n132: \n133: // This list should be exactly the same as the codes iota defined above in the same order.\n134: var codes = []string{\"Success\", \"Error\", \"Unschedulable\", \"UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\", \"Wait\", \"Skip\", \"Pending\"}\n135: \n136: func (c Code) String() string {\n137: \treturn codes[c]\n138: }\n139: \n140: const (\n141: \t// MaxNodeScore is the maximum score a Score plugin is expected to return.\n142: \tMaxNodeScore int64 = 100\n143: \n144: \t// MinNodeScore is the minimum score a Score plugin is expected to return.\n145: \tMinNodeScore int64 = 0\n146: \n147: \t// MaxTotalScore is the maximum total score.\n148: \tMaxTotalScore int64 = math.MaxInt64\n149: )\n150: \n151: // PodsToActivateKey is a reserved state key for stashing pods.\n152: // If the stashed pods are present in unschedulablePods or backoffQ，they will be\n153: // activated (i.e., moved to activeQ) in two phases:\n154: // - end of a scheduling cycle if it succeeds (will be cleared from `PodsToActivate` if activated)\n155: // - end of a binding cycle if it succeeds\n156: var PodsToActivateKey StateKey = \"kubernetes.io/pods-to-activate\"\n157: \n158: // PodsToActivate stores pods to be activated.\n159: type PodsToActivate struct {\n160: \tsync.Mutex\n161: \t// Map is keyed with namespaced pod name, and valued with the pod.\n162: \tMap map[string]*v1.Pod\n163: }\n164: \n165: // Clone just returns the same state.\n166: func (s *PodsToActivate) Clone() StateData {\n167: \treturn s\n168: }\n169: \n170: // NewPodsToActivate instantiates a PodsToActivate object.\n171: func NewPodsToActivate() *PodsToActivate {\n172: \treturn &PodsToActivate{Map: make(map[string]*v1.Pod)}\n173: }\n174: \n175: // Status indicates the result of running a plugin. It consists of a code, a\n176: // message, (optionally) an error, and a plugin name it fails by.\n177: // When the status code is not Success, the reasons should explain why.\n178: // And, when code is Success, all the other fields should be empty.\n179: // NOTE: A nil Status is also considered as Success.\n180: type Status struct {\n181: \tcode    Code\n182: \treasons []string\n183: \terr     error\n184: \t// plugin is an optional field that records the plugin name causes this status.\n185: \t// It's set by the framework when code is Unschedulable, UnschedulableAndUnresolvable or Pending.\n186: \tplugin string\n187: }\n188: \n189: func (s *Status) WithError(err error) *Status {\n190: \ts.err = err\n191: \treturn s\n192: }\n193: \n194: // Code returns code of the Status.\n195: func (s *Status) Code() Code {\n196: \tif s == nil {\n197: \t\treturn Success\n198: \t}\n199: \treturn s.code\n200: }\n201: \n202: // Message returns a concatenated message on reasons of the Status.\n203: func (s *Status) Message() string {\n204: \tif s == nil {\n205: \t\treturn \"\"\n206: \t}\n207: \treturn strings.Join(s.Reasons(), \", \")\n208: }\n209: \n210: // SetPlugin sets the given plugin name to s.plugin.\n211: func (s *Status) SetPlugin(plugin string) {\n212: \ts.plugin = plugin\n213: }\n214: \n215: // WithPlugin sets the given plugin name to s.plugin,\n216: // and caused this status.\n223: func (s *Status) Plugin() string {\n224: \treturn s.plugin\n225: }\n226: \n227: // Reasons returns reasons of the Status.\n228: func (s *Status) Reasons() []string {\n229: \tif s.err != nil {\n230: \t\treturn append([]string{s.err.Error()}, s.reasons...)\n231: \t}\n232: \treturn s.reasons\n233: }\n234: \n235: // AppendReason appends given reason to the Status.\n236: func (s *Status) AppendReason(reason string) {\n237: \ts.reasons = append(s.reasons, reason)\n238: }\n239: \n240: // IsSuccess returns true if and only if \"Status\" is nil or Code is \"Success\".\n241: func (s *Status) IsSuccess() bool {\n242: \treturn s.Code() == Success\n243: }\n244: \n245: // IsWait returns true if and only if \"Status\" is non-nil and its Code is \"Wait\".\n246: func (s *Status) IsWait() bool {\n247: \treturn s.Code() == Wait\n248: }\n249: \n250: // IsSkip returns true if and only if \"Status\" is non-nil and its Code is \"Skip\".\n251: func Pending).\n256: func (s *Status) IsRejected() bool {\n257: \tcode := s.Code()\n258: \treturn code == Unschedulable || code == UnschedulableAndUnresolvable || code == Pending\n259: }\n260: \n261: // AsError returns nil if the status is a success, a wait or a skip; otherwise returns an \"error\" object\n262: // with a concatenated message on reasons of the Status.\n263: func (s *Status) AsError() error {\n264: \tif s.IsSuccess() || s.IsWait() || s.IsSkip() {\n265: \t\treturn nil\n266: \t}\n267: \tif s.err != nil {\n268: \t\treturn s.err\n269: \t}\n270: \treturn errors.New(s.Message())\n271: }\n272: \n273: // Equal checks equality of two statuses. This is useful for testing with\n274: // cmp.Equal.\n275: func (s *Status) Equal(x *Status) bool {\n276: \tif s == nil || x == nil {\n277: \t\treturn s.IsSuccess() && x.IsSuccess()\n278: \t}\n279: \tif s.code != x.code {\n280: \t\treturn false\n281: \t}\n282: \tif !cmp.Equal(s.err, x.err, cmpopts.EquateErrors()) {\n283: \t\treturn false\n284: \t}\n285: \tif !cmp.Equal(s.reasons, x.reasons) {\n286: \t\treturn false\n287: \t}\n288: \treturn cmp.Equal(s.plugin, x.plugin)\n289: }\n290: \n291: func (s *Status) String() string {\n292: \treturn s.Message()\n293: }\n294: \n295: // NewStatus reasons,\n300: \t}\n301: \treturn s\n302: }\n303: \n304: // AsStatus wraps an error in a Status.\n305: func AsStatus(err error) *Status {\n306: \tif err == nil {\n307: \t\treturn nil\n308: \t}\n309: Plugin is the parent type for all the scheduling framework plugins.\n330: type Plugin interface {\n331: \tName() string\n332: }\n333: \n334: // PreEnqueuePlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \"PreEnqueue\" plugins.\n335: // These plugins are called prior to adding Pods to activeQ.\n336: // Note: an preEnqueue plugin is expected to be lightweight and efficient, so it's not expected to\n337: // involve expensive calls like accessing external endpoints; otherwise it'd block other\n338: // Pods' enqueuing in event handlers.\n339: type PreEnqueuePlugin interface {\n340: \tPlugin\n341: \t// PreEnqueue is called prior to adding Pods to activeQ.\n342: \tPreEnqueue(ctx context.Context, p *v1.Pod) *Status\n343: }\n344: \n345: // LessFunc is the function to sort pod info\n346: type LessFunc func(podInfo1, podInfo2 *QueuedPodInfo) bool\n347: \n348: // QueueSortPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \"QueueSort\" plugins.\n349: // These plugins are used to sort pods in the scheduling queue. Only one queue sort\n350: // plugin may be enabled at a time.\n351: type QueueSortPlugin interface {\n352: \tPlugin\n353: \t// Less are used to sort pods in the scheduling queue.\n354: \tLess(*QueuedPodInfo, *QueuedPodInfo) bool\n355: }\n356: \n357: // EnqueueExtensions is an optional interface that plugins can implement to efficiently\n358: // move unschedulable Pods in internal scheduling queues.\n359: // In the scheduler, Pods can be unschedulable by PreEnqueue, PreFilter, Filter, Reserve, and Permit plugins,\n360: // and Pods rejected by these plugins are requeued based on this extension point.\n361: // Failures from other extension points are regarded as temporal errors (e.g., network failure),\n362: // and the scheduler requeue Pods without this extension point - always requeue Pods to activeQ after backoff.\n363: // This is because such temporal errors cannot be resolved by specific cluster events,\n364: // and we have no choise but keep retrying scheduling until the failure is resolved.\n365: //\n366: // Plugins that make pod unschedulable (PreEnqueue, PreFilter, Filter, Reserve, and Permit plugins) should implement this interface,\n367: // otherwise the default implementation will be used, which is less efficient in requeueing Pods rejected by the plugin.\n368: // And, if plugins other than above extension points support this interface, they are just ignored.\n369: type EnqueueExtensions interface {\n370: \tPlugin\n371: \t// EventsToRegister returns a series of possible events that may cause a Pod\n372: \t// failed by this plugin schedulable. Each event has a callback function that\n373: \t// filters out events to reduce useless retry of Pod's scheduling.\n374: \t// The events will be registered when instantiating the internal scheduling queue,\n375: \t// and leveraged to build event handlers dynamically.\n376: \t// Note: the returned list needs to be static (not depend on configuration parameters);\n377: \t// otherwise it would lead to undefined behavior.\n378: \t//\n379: \t// Appropriate implementation of this function will make Pod's re-scheduling accurate and performant.\n380: \tEventsToRegister() []ClusterEventWithHint\n381: }\n382: \n383: // PreFilterExtensions is an interface that is included in plugins that allow specifying\n384: // callbacks to make incremental updates to its supposedly pre-calculated\n385: // state.\n386: type PreFilterExtensions interface {\n387: \t// AddPod is called by the framework while trying to evaluate the impact\n388: \t// of adding podToAdd to the node while scheduling podToSchedule.\n389: \tAddPod(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, podToSchedule *v1.Pod, podInfoToAdd *PodInfo, nodeInfo *NodeInfo) *Status\n390: \t// RemovePod is called by the framework while trying to evaluate the impact\n391: \t// of removing podToRemove from the node while scheduling podToSchedule.\n392: \tRemovePod(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, podToSchedule *v1.Pod, podInfoToRemove *PodInfo, nodeInfo *NodeInfo) *Status\n393: }\n394: \n395: // PreFilterPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \"PreFilter\" plugins.\n396: // These plugins are called at the beginning of the scheduling cycle.\n397: type PreFilterPlugin interface {\n398: \tPlugin\n399: \t// PreFilter is called at the beginning of the scheduling cycle. All PreFilter\n400: \t// plugins must return success or the pod will be rejected. PreFilter could optionally\n401: \t// return a PreFilterResult to influence which nodes to evaluate downstream. This is useful\n402: \t// for cases where it is possible to determine the subset of nodes to process in O(1) time.\n403: \t// When PreFilterResult filters out some Nodes, the framework considers Nodes that are filtered out as getting \"UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\".\n404: \t// i.e., those Nodes will be out of the candidates of the preemption.\n405: \t//\n406: \t// When it returns Skip status, returned PreFilterResult and other fields in status are just ignored,\n407: \t// and coupled Filter plugin/PreFilterExtensions() will be skipped in this scheduling cycle.\n408: \tPreFilter(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod) (*PreFilterResult, *Status)\n409: \t// PreFilterExtensions returns a PreFilterExtensions interface if the plugin implements one,\n410: \t// or nil if it does not. A Pre-filter plugin can provide extensions to incrementally\n411: \t// modify its pre-processed info. The framework guarantees that the extensions\n412: \t// AddPod/RemovePod will only be called after PreFilter, possibly on a cloned\n413: \t// CycleState, and may call those functions more than once before calling\n414: \t// Filter again on a specific node.\n415: \tPreFilterExtensions() PreFilterExtensions\n416: }\n417: \n418: // FilterPlugin is an interface for Filter plugins. These plugins are called at the\n419: // filter extension point for filtering out hosts that cannot run a pod.\n420: // This concept used to be called 'predicate' in the original scheduler.\n421: // These plugins should return \"Success\", \"Unschedulable\" or \"Error\" in Status.code.\n422: // However, the scheduler accepts other valid codes as well.\n423: // Anything other than \"Success\" will lead to exclusion of the given host from\n424: // running the pod.\n425: type FilterPlugin interface {\n426: \tPlugin\n427: \t// Filter is called by the scheduling framework.\n428: \t// All FilterPlugins should return \"Success\" to declare that\n429: \t// the given node fits the pod. If Filter doesn't return \"Success\",\n430: \t// it will return \"Unschedulable\", \"UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\" or \"Error\".\n431: \t// For the node being evaluated, Filter plugins should look at the passed\n432: \t// nodeInfo reference for this particular node's information (e.g., pods\n433: \t// considered to be running on the node) instead of looking it up in the\n434: \t// NodeInfoSnapshot because we don't guarantee that they will be the same.\n435: \t// For example, during preemption, we may pass a copy of the original\n436: \t// nodeInfo object that has some pods removed from it to evaluate the\n437: \t// possibility of preempting them to schedule the target pod.\n438: \tFilter(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, nodeInfo *NodeInfo) *Status\n439: }\n440: \n441: // PostFilterPlugin is an interface for \"PostFilter\" plugins. These plugins are called\n442: // after a pod cannot be scheduled.\n443: type PostFilterPlugin interface {\n444: \tPlugin\n445: \t// PostFilter is called by the scheduling framework\n446: \t// when the scheduling cycle failed at PreFilter or Filter by Unschedulable or UnschedulableAndUnresolvable.\n447: \t// NodeToStatusMap has statuses that each Node got in the Filter phase.\n448: \t// If this scheduling cycle failed at PreFilter, all Nodes have the status from the rejector PreFilter plugin in NodeToStatusMap.\n449: \t// Note that the scheduling framework runs PostFilter plugins even when PreFilter returned UnschedulableAndUnresolvable.\n450: \t// In that case, NodeToStatusMap contains all Nodes with UnschedulableAndUnresolvable.\n451: \t//\n452: \t// Also, ignoring Nodes with UnschedulableAndUnresolvable is the responsibility of each PostFilter plugin,\n453: \t// meaning NodeToStatusMap obviously could have Nodes with UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\n454: \t// and the scheduling framework does call PostFilter even when all Nodes in NodeToStatusMap are UnschedulableAndUnresolvable.\n455: \t//\n456: \t// A PostFilter plugin should return one of the following statuses:\n457: \t// - Unschedulable: the plugin gets executed successfully but the pod cannot be made schedulable.\n458: \t// - Success: the plugin gets executed successfully and the pod can be made schedulable.\n459: \t// - Error: the plugin aborts due to some internal error.\n460: \t//\n461: \t// Informational plugins should be configured ahead of other ones, and always return Unschedulable status.\n462: \t// Optionally, a non-nil PostFilterResult may be returned along with a Success status. NodeScoreList declares a list of nodes and their scores.\ntype NodeScoreList []NodeScore\n\n// NodeScore is a struct with node name and score.\ntype NodeScore struct {\n\tName  string\n\tScore int64\n}\n\n// NodeToStatusMap declares map from node name to its status.\ntype NodeToStatusMap map[string]*Status\n\n// NodePluginScores is a struct with node name and scores for that node.\ntype NodePluginScores struct {\n\t// Name is node name.\n\tName string\n\t// Scores is scores from plugins and extenders.\n\tScores []PluginScore\n\t// TotalScore is the total score in int64\n}\n\n// Code is the Status code/type which is returned from plugins.\ntype Code int\n\n// These are predefined codes used in a Status.\n// Note: when you add a new status, you have to add it in `codes` slice below.\nconst (\n\t// Success means that plugin ran correctly and found pod schedulable.\n\t// NOTE: A nil status is also considered as \"Success\".\n\tSuccess Code = iota\n\t// Error is one of the failures, used for internal plugin errors, unexpected input, etc.\n\t// Plugin shouldn't return this code for expected failures, like Unschedulable.\n\t// Since it's the unexpected failure, the scheduling queue registers the pod without unschedulable plugins.\n\t// Meaning, the Pod will be requeued to activeQ/backoffQ soon.\n\tError\n\t// Unschedulable is one of the failures, used when a plugin finds a pod unschedulable.\n\t// If it's returned from PreFilter or Filter, the scheduler might attempt to\n\t// run other postFilter plugins like preemption to get this pod scheduled.\n\t// Use UnschedulableAndUnresolvable to make the scheduler skipping other postFilter plugins.\n\t// The accompanying status message should explain why the pod is unschedulable.\n\t//\n\t// We regard the backoff as a penalty of wasting the scheduling cycle.\n\t// When the scheduling queue requeues Pods, which was rejected with Unschedulable in the last scheduling,\n\t// the Pod goes through backoff.\n\tUnschedulable\n\t// UnschedulableAndUnresolvable is used when a plugin finds a pod unschedulable and\n\t// other postFilter plugins like preemption would not change anything.\n\t// See the comment on PostFilter interface for more details about how PostFilter should handle this status.\n\t// Plugins should return Unschedulable if it is possible that the pod can get scheduled\n\t// after running other postFilter plugins.\n\t// The accompanying status message should explain why the pod is unschedulable.\n\t//\n\t// We regard the backoff as a penalty of wasting the scheduling cycle.\n\t// When the scheduling queue requeues Pods, which was rejected with UnschedulableAndUnresolvable in the last scheduling,\n\t// the Pod goes through backoff.\n\tUnschedulableAndUnresolvable\n\t// Wait is used when a Permit plugin finds a pod scheduling should wait.\n\tWait\n\t// Skip is used in the following scenarios:\n\t// - when a Bind plugin chooses to skip binding.\n\t// - when a PreFilter plugin returns Skip so that coupled Filter plugin/PreFilterExtensions() will be skipped.\n\t// - when a PreScore plugin returns Skip so that coupled Score plugin will be skipped.\n\tSkip\n\t// Pending means that the scheduling process is finished successfully,\n\t// but the plugin wants to stop the scheduling cycle/binding cycle here.\n\t//\n\t// For example, the DRA plugin sometimes needs to wait for the external device driver\n\t// to provision the resource for the Pod.\n\t// It's different from when to return Unschedulable/UnschedulableAndUnresolvable,\n\t// because in this case, the scheduler decides where the Pod can go successfully,\n\t// but we need to wait for the external component to do something based on that scheduling result.\n\t//\n\t// We regard the backoff as a penalty of wasting the scheduling cycle.\n\t// In the case of returning Pending, we cannot say the scheduling cycle is wasted\n\t// because the scheduling result is used to proceed the Pod's scheduling forward,\n\t// that particular scheduling cycle is failed though.\n\t// So, Pods rejected by such reasons don't need to suffer a penalty (backoff).\n\t// When the scheduling queue requeues Pods, which was rejected with Pending in the last scheduling,\n\t// the Pod goes to activeQ directly ignoring backoff.\n\tPending\n)\n\n// This list should be exactly the same as the codes iota defined above in the same order.\nvar codes = []string{\"Success\", \"Error\", \"Unschedulable\", \"UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\", \"Wait\", \"Skip\", \"Pending\"}\n\nfunc (c Code) String() string {\n\treturn codes[c]\n}\n\nconst (\n\t// MaxNodeScore is the maximum score a Score plugin is score.\n\tMaxTotalScore int64 = math.MaxInt64\n)\n\n// PodsToActivateKey is a reserved state key for stashing pods.\n// If the stashed pods are present in unschedulablePods or backoffQ，they will be\n// activated (i.e., moved to activeQ) in two phases:\n// - end of a scheduling cycle if it succeeds (will be cleared from `PodsToActivate` if activated)\n// - end of a binding cycle if it succeeds\nvar PodsToActivateKey StateKey = \"kubernetes.io/pods-to-activate\"\n\n// PodsToActivate stores pods to be activated.\ntype PodsToActivate struct {\n\tsync.Mutex\n\t// Map is keyed with instantiates a PodsToActivate object.\nfunc NewPodsToActivate() *PodsToActivate {\n\treturn &PodsToActivate{Map: make(map[string]*v1.Pod)}\n}\n\n// Status indicates the result of running a plugin. It consists of a code, a\n// message, (optionally) an error, and a plugin name it fails by.\n// When the status code is not Success, the reasons should explain why.\n// And, when code is Success, all the other fields should be empty.\n// NOTE: A nil Status is also considered as Success.\ntype Status struct {\n\tcode    Code\n\treasons []string\n\terr     error\n\t// plugin is an optional field that records the plugin name causes this status.\n\t// It's set by the framework when code is Unschedulable, UnschedulableAndUnresolvable or Pending.\n\tplugin string\n}\n\nfunc (s *Status) WithError(err error) *Status {\n\ts.err = err\n\treturn s\n}\n\n// Code returns code of the Status.\nfunc (s *Status) Code() Code {\n\tif s == nil {\n\t\treturn Success\n\t}\n\treturn s.code\n}\n\n// given status object.\nfunc (s *Status) WithPlugin(plugin string) *Status {\n\ts.SetPlugin(plugin)\n\treturn s\n}\n\n// Plugin returns the plugin name which caused this status.\nfunc (s *Status) Plugin() string {\n\treturn s.plugin\n}\n\n// Reasons returns reasons of the Status.\nfunc (s *Status) Reasons() []string {\n\tif s.err != nil {\n\t\treturn append([]string{s.err.Error()}, s.reasons...)\n\t}\n\treturn s.reasons\n}\n\n// AppendReason appends given reason to the Status.\nfunc (s *Status) AppendReason(reason string) {\n\ts.reasons = append(s.reasons, reason)\n}\n\n// IsSuccess returns true if and only if \"Status\" is nil or Code is \"Success\".\nfunc (s *Status) IsSuccess() bool {\n\treturn s.Code() == Success\n}\n\n// IsWait returns true if and only if \"Status\" is non-nil and its Code is \"Wait\".\nfunc (s *Status) IsWait() bool {\n\treturn s.Code() == Wait\n}\n\n// IsSkip returns true if and only if \"Status\" is non-nil and its Code is \"Skip\".\nfunc (s *Status) IsSkip() bool {\n\treturn s.Code() == Skip\n}\n\n// IsRejected returns true if \"Status\" is Unschedulable (Unschedulable, UnschedulableAndUnresolvable, or Pending).\nfunc (s *Status) IsRejected() bool {\n\tcode := s.Code()\n\treturn code == Unschedulable || code == UnschedulableAndUnresolvable || code == Pending\n}\n\n// AsError returns nil if the status is a success, a wait or a skip; otherwise returns an \"error\" object\n// with a concatenated message on reasons of the Status.\nfunc (s *Status) AsError() error {\n\tif s.IsSuccess() || s.IsWait() || s.IsSkip() {\n\t\treturn nil\n\t}\n\tif s.err != nil {\n\t\treturn s.err\n\t}\n\treturn errors.New(s.Message())\n}\n\n// Equal checks equality of two statuses. This is useful for testing with\n// cmp.Equal.\nfunc (s *Status) Equal(x *Status) bool {\n\tif s == nil || x == nil {\n\t\treturn s.IsSuccess() && x.IsSuccess()\n\t}\n\tif s.code != x.code {\n\t\treturn false\n\t}\n\tif !cmp.Equal(s.err, x.err, cmpopts.EquateErrors()) {\n\t\treturn false\n\t}\n\tif !cmp.Equal(s.reasons, x.reasons) {\n\t\treturn false\n\t}\n\treturn cmp.Equal(s.plugin, x.plugin)\n}\n\nfunc (s *Status) String() string {\n\treturn s.Message()\n}\n\n// NewStatus makes a Status out of the given arguments and returns its pointer.\nfunc NewStatus(code Code, reasons ...string) *Status {\n\ts := &Status{\n\t\tcode:    code,\n\t\treasons: reasons,\n\t}\n\treturn s\n}\n\n// AsStatus wraps an error in a Status.\nfunc AsStatus(err error) *Status {\n\tif err == nil {\n\t\treturn nil\n\t}\n\treturn &Status{\n\t\tcode: Error,\n\t\terr:  err,\n\t}\n}\n\n// WaitingPod represents a pod currently waiting in the permit phase.\ntype WaitingPod interface {\n\t// GetPod returns a reference to the waiting pod.\n\tGetPod() *v1.Pod\n\t// GetPendingPlugins returns a list of pending Permit plugin's name.\n\tGetPendingPlugins() []string\n\t// Allow declares the waiting pod is allowed to be scheduled by the plugin named as \"pluginName\".\n\t// If this is the last remaining plugin to allow, then a success signal is delivered\n\t// to unblock the pod.\n\tAllow(pluginName string)\n\t// Reject declares the waiting pod unschedulable.\n\tReject(pluginName, msg string)\n}\n\n// Plugin is the parent type for all the scheduling framework plugins.\ntype Plugin interface {\n\tName() string\n}\n\n// PreEnqueuePlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \"PreEnqueue\" plugins.\n// These plugins are called prior to adding Pods to activeQ.\n// Note: an preEnqueue plugin is expected to be lightweight and efficient, so it's not expected to\n// involve expensive calls like accessing external endpoints; otherwise it'd block other\n// Pods' enqueuing in event handlers.\ntype PreEnqueuePlugin interface {\n\tPlugin\n\t// PreEnqueue is called prior to adding Pods to activeQ.\n\tPreEnqueue(ctx context.Context, p *v1.Pod) *Status\n}\n\n// LessFunc is the function to sort pod info\ntype LessFunc func(podInfo1, podInfo2 *QueuedPodInfo) bool\n\n// QueueSortPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \"QueueSort\" plugins.\n// These plugins are used to sort pods in the scheduling queue. Only one queue sort\n// plugin may be enabled at a time.\ntype QueueSortPlugin interface {\n\tPlugin\n\t// Less are used to sort pods in the scheduling queue.\n\tLess(*QueuedPodInfo, *QueuedPodInfo) bool\n}\n\n// EnqueueExtensions is an optional interface that plugins can implement to efficiently\n// move unschedulable Pods in internal scheduling queues.\n// In the scheduler, Pods can be unschedulable by PreEnqueue, PreFilter, Filter, Reserve, and Permit plugins,\n// and Pods rejected by these plugins are requeued based on this extension point.\n// Failures from other extension points are regarded as temporal errors (e.g., network failure),\n// and the scheduler requeue Pods without this extension point - always requeue Pods to activeQ after backoff.\n// This is because such temporal errors cannot be resolved by specific cluster events,\n// and we have no choise but keep retrying scheduling until the failure is resolved.\n//\n// Plugins that make pod unschedulable (PreEnqueue, PreFilter, Filter, Reserve, and Permit plugins) should implement this interface,\n// otherwise the default implementation will be used, which is less efficient in requeueing Pods rejected by the plugin.\n// And, if plugins other than above extension points support this interface, they are just ignored.\ntype EnqueueExtensions interface {\n\tPlugin\n\t// EventsToRegister returns a series of possible events that may cause a Pod\n\t// failed by this plugin schedulable. Each event has a callback function that\n\t// filters out events to reduce useless retry of Pod's scheduling.\n\t// The events will be registered when instantiating the internal scheduling queue,\n\t// and leveraged to build event handlers dynamically.\n\t// Note: the returned list needs to be static (not depend on configuration parameters);\n\t// otherwise it would lead to undefined behavior.\n\t//\n\t// Appropriate implementation of this function will make Pod's re-scheduling accurate and performant.\n\tEventsToRegister() []ClusterEventWithHint\n}\n\n// PreFilterExtensions is an interface that is included in plugins that allow specifying\n// callbacks to make incremental updates to its supposedly pre-calculated\n// state.\ntype PreFilterExtensions interface {\n\t// AddPod is called by the framework while trying to evaluate the impact\n\t// of adding podToAdd to the node while scheduling podToSchedule.\n\tAddPod(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, podToSchedule *v1.Pod, podInfoToAdd *PodInfo, nodeInfo *NodeInfo) *Status\n\t// RemovePod is called by the framework while trying to evaluate the impact\n\t// of removing podToRemove from the node while scheduling podToSchedule.\n\tRemovePod(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, podToSchedule *v1.Pod, podInfoToRemove *PodInfo, nodeInfo *NodeInfo) *Status\n}\n\n// PreFilterPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \"PreFilter\" plugins.\n// These plugins are called at the beginning of the scheduling cycle.\ntype PreFilterPlugin interface {\n\tPlugin\n\t// PreFilter is called at the beginning of the scheduling cycle. All PreFilter\n\t// plugins must return success or the pod will be rejected. PreFilter could optionally\n\t// return a PreFilterResult to influence which nodes to evaluate downstream. This is useful\n\t// for cases where it is possible to determine the subset of nodes to process in O(1) time.\n\t// When PreFilterResult filters out some Nodes, the framework considers Nodes that are filtered out as getting \"UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\".\n\t// i.e., those Nodes will be out of the candidates of the preemption.\n\t//\n\t// When it returns Skip status, returned PreFilterResult and other fields in status are just ignored,\n\t// and coupled Filter plugin/PreFilterExtensions() will be skipped in this scheduling cycle.\n\tPreFilter(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod) (*PreFilterResult, *Status)\n\t// PreFilterExtensions returns a PreFilterExtensions interface if the plugin implements one,\n\t// or nil if it does not. A Pre-filter plugin can provide extensions to incrementally\n\t// modify its pre-processed info. The framework guarantees that the extensions\n\t// AddPod/RemovePod will only be called after PreFilter, possibly on a cloned\n\t// CycleState, and may call those functions more than once before calling\n\t// Filter again on a specific node.\n\tPreFilterExtensions() PreFilterExtensions\n}\n\n// FilterPlugin is an interface for Filter plugins. These plugins are called at the\n// filter extension point for filtering out hosts that cannot run a pod.\n// This concept used to be called 'predicate' in the original scheduler.\n// These plugins should return \"Success\", \"Unschedulable\" or \"Error\" in Status.code.\n// However, the scheduler accepts other valid codes as well.\n// Anything other than \"Success\" will lead to exclusion of the given host from\n// running the pod.\ntype FilterPlugin interface {\n\tPlugin\n\t// Filter is called by the scheduling framework.\n\t// All FilterPlugins should return \"Success\" to declare that\n\t// the given node fits the pod. If Filter doesn't return \"Success\",\n\t// it will return \"Unschedulable\", \"UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\" or \"Error\".\n\t// For the node being evaluated, Filter plugins should look at the passed\n\t// nodeInfo reference for this particular node's information (e.g., pods\n\t// considered to be running on the node) instead of looking it up in the\n\t// NodeInfoSnapshot because we don't guarantee that they will be the same.\n\t// For example, during preemption, we may pass a copy of the original\n\t// nodeInfo object that has some pods removed from it to evaluate the\n\t// possibility of preempting them to schedule the target pod.\n\tFilter(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, nodeInfo *NodeInfo) *Status\n}\n\n// PostFilterPlugin is an interface for \"PostFilter\" plugins. These plugins are called\n// after a pod cannot be scheduled.\ntype PostFilterPlugin interface {\n\tPlugin\n\t// PostFilter is called by the scheduling framework\n\t// when the scheduling cycle failed at PreFilter or Filter by Unschedulable or UnschedulableAndUnresolvable.\n\t// NodeToStatusMap has statuses that each Node got in the Filter phase.\n\t// If this scheduling cycle failed at PreFilter, all Nodes have the status from the rejector PreFilter plugin in NodeToStatusMap.\n\t// Note that the scheduling framework runs PostFilter plugins even when PreFilter returned UnschedulableAndUnresolvable.\n\t// In that case, NodeToStatusMap contains all Nodes with UnschedulableAndUnresolvable.\n\t//\n\t// Also, ignoring Nodes with UnschedulableAndUnresolvable is the responsibility of each PostFilter plugin,\n\t// meaning NodeToStatusMap obviously could have Nodes with UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\n\t// and the scheduling framework does call PostFilter even when all Nodes in NodeToStatusMap are UnschedulableAndUnresolvable.\n\t//\n\t// A PostFilter plugin should return one of the following statuses:\n\t// - Unschedulable: the plugin gets executed successfully but the pod cannot be made schedulable.\n\t// - Success: the plugin gets executed successfully and the pod can be made schedulable.\n\t// - Error: the plugin aborts due to some internal error.\n\t//\n\t// Informational plugins should be configured ahead of other ones, and always return Unschedulable status.\n\t// Optionally, a non-nil PostFilterResult may be returned along with a Success status. For example,\n\t// a preemption plugin may choose to return nominatedNodeName, so that framework can reuse that to update the\n\t// preemptor pod's .spec.status.nominatedNodeName field.\n\tPostFilter(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, filteredNodeStatusMap NodeToStatusMap) (*PostFilterResult, *Status)\n}\n\n// PreScorePlugin is an interface for \"PreScore\" plugin. PreScore is an\n// informational extension point. Plugins will be called with a list of nodes\n// that passed the filtering phase. A plugin may use this data to update internal\n// state or to generate logs/metrics.\ntype PreScorePlugin interface {\n\tPlugin\n\t// PreScore is called by the scheduling framework after a list of nodes\n\t// passed the filtering phase. All prescore plugins must return success or\n\t// the pod will be rejected\n\t// When it returns Skip status, other fields in status are just ignored,\n\t// and coupled Score plugin will be skipped in this scheduling cycle.\n\tPreScore(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, nodes []*NodeInfo) *Status\n}\n\n// ScoreNormalizer is an interface for Score normalization functionality.\ntype ScoreNormalizer interface {\n\t// NormalizeScore is called for all node scores produced by the same plugin's \"Score\"\n\t// method. A successful run of NormalizeScore will update the scores list and return\n\t// a success status.\n\tNormalizeScore(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod, scores NodeScoreList) *Status\n}\n\n// ScorePlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \"Score\" plugins to rank\n// nodes that passed the filtering phase.\ntype ScorePlugin interface {\n\tPlugin\n\t// Score is called on each filtered node. It must return success and an integer\n\t// indicating the rank of the node. All scoring plugins must return success or\n\t// the pod will be rejected.\n\tScore(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string) (int64, *Status)\n\n\t// ScoreNormalizer returns a ScoreNormalizer interface if it implements one, or nil if does not.\n\tScoreNormalizer() ScoreNormalizer\n}\n\n// ReservePlugin is an interface for plugins with Reserve and Unreserve\n// methods. These are meant to update the state of the plugin. This concept\n// used to be called 'assume' in the original scheduler. These plugins should\n// return only Success or Error in Status.code. However, the scheduler accepts\n// other valid codes as well. Anything other than Success will lead to\n// rejection of the pod.\ntype ReservePlugin interface {\n\tPlugin\n\t// Reserve is called by the scheduling framework when the scheduler cache is\n\t// updated. If this method returns a failed Status, the scheduler will call\n\t// the Unreserve method for all enabled ReservePlugins.\n\tReserve(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string) *Status\n\t// Unreserve is called by the scheduling framework when a reserved pod was\n\t// rejected, an error occurred during reservation of subsequent plugins, or\n\t// in a later phase. The Unreserve method implementation must be idempotent\n\t// and may be called by the scheduler even if the corresponding Reserve\n\t// method for the same plugin was not called.\n\tUnreserve(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string)\n}\n\n// PreBindPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \"PreBind\" plugins.\n// These plugins are called before a pod being scheduled.\ntype PreBindPlugin interface {\n\tPlugin\n\t// PreBind is called before binding a pod. All prebind plugins must return\n\t// success or the pod will be rejected and won't be sent for binding.\n\tPreBind(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string) *Status\n}\n\n// PostBindPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \"PostBind\" plugins.\n// These plugins are called after a pod is successfully bound to a node.\ntype PostBindPlugin interface {\n\tPlugin\n\t// PostBind is called after a pod is successfully bound. These plugins are\n\t// informational. A common application of this extension point is for cleaning\n\t// up. If a plugin needs to clean-up its state after a pod is scheduled and\n\t// bound, PostBind is the extension point that it should register.\n\tPostBind(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string)\n}\n\n// PermitPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \"Permit\" plugins.\n// These plugins are called before a pod is bound to a node.\ntype PermitPlugin interface {\n\tPlugin\n\t// Permit is called before binding a pod (and before prebind plugins). Permit\n\t// plugins are used to prevent or delay the binding of a Pod. A permit plugin\n\t// must return success or wait with timeout duration, or the pod will be rejected.\n\t// The pod will also be rejected if the wait timeout or the pod is rejected while\n\t// waiting. Note that if the plugin returns \"wait\", the framework will wait only\n\t// after running the remaining plugins given that no other plugin rejects the pod.\n\tPermit(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string) (*Status, time.Duration)\n}\n\n// BindPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \"Bind\" plugins. Bind\n// plugins are used to bind a pod to a Node.\ntype BindPlugin interface {\n\tPlugin\n\t// Bind plugins will not be called until all pre-bind plugins have completed. Each\n\t// bind plugin is called in the configured order. A bind plugin may choose whether\n\t// or not to handle the given Pod. If a bind plugin chooses to handle a Pod, the\n\t// remaining bind plugins are skipped. When a bind plugin does not handle a pod,\n\t// it must return Skip in its Status code. If a bind plugin returns an Error, the\n\t// pod is rejected and will not be bound.\n\tBind(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string) *Status\n}\n\n// Framework manages the set of plugins in use by the scheduling framework.\n// Configured plugins are called at specified points in a scheduling context.\ntype Framework interface {\n\tHandle\n\n\t// PreEnqueuePlugins returns the registered preEnqueue plugins.\n\tPreEnqueuePlugins() []PreEnqueuePlugin\n\n\t// EnqueueExtensions returns the registered Enqueue extensions.\n\tEnqueueExtensions() []EnqueueExtensions\n\n\t// QueueSortFunc returns the function to sort pods in scheduling queue\n\tQueueSortFunc() LessFunc\n\n\t// RunPreFilterPlugins runs the set of configured PreFilter plugins. It returns\n\t// *Status and its code is set to non-success if any of the plugins returns\n\t// anything but Success. If a non-success status is returned, then the scheduling\n\t// cycle is aborted.\n\t// It also returns a PreFilterResult, which may influence what or how many nodes to\n\t// evaluate downstream.\n\tRunPreFilterPlugins(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, pod *v1.Pod) (*PreFilterResult, *Status)\n\n\t// RunPostFilterPlugins runs the set of configured PostFilter plugins.\n\t// PostFilter plugins can either be informational, in which case should be configured\n\t// to execute first and return Unschedulable status, or ones that try to change the\n\t// cluster state to make the pod potentially schedulable in a future scheduling cycle.\n\tRunPostFilterPlugins(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, filteredNodeStatusMap NodeToStatusMap) (*PostFilterResult, *Status)\n\n\t// RunPreBindPlugins runs the set of configured PreBind plugins. If the Status code is \"Unschedulable\", it is\n\t// considered as a scheduling check failure, otherwise, it is considered as an\n\t// internal error. In either case the pod is not going to be bound.\n\tRunPreBindPlugins(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, nodeName string) *Status\n\n\t// RunPostBindPlugins runs the set of configured PostBind plugins.\n\tRunPostBindPlugins(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, nodeName string)\n\n\t// RunReservePluginsReserve runs the Reserve method of the set of\n\t// configured Reserve plugins. If any of these calls returns an error, it\n\t// does not continue running the remaining ones and returns the error. In\n\t// such case, pod will not be scheduled.\n\tRunReservePluginsReserve(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, nodeName string) *Status\n\n\t// RunReservePluginsUnreserve runs the Unreserve method of the set of\n\t// configured Reserve plugins.\n\tRunReservePluginsUnreserve(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, nodeName string)\n\n\t// RunPermitPlugins runs the set of configured Permit plugins. int64\n}\n\n// Code is the Status code/type which is returned from plugins.\ntype Code int\n\n// These are predefined codes used in a Status.\n// Note: when you add a new status, you have to add it in `codes` slice below.\nconst (\n\t// Success means that plugin ran correctly and found pod schedulable.\n\t// NOTE: A nil status is also considered as \"Success\".\n\tSuccess Code = iota\n\t// Error is one of the failures, used for internal plugin errors, unexpected input, etc.\n\t// Plugin shouldn't return this code for expected failures, like Unschedulable.\n\t// Since it's the unexpected failure, the scheduling queue registers the pod without unschedulable plugins.\n\t// Meaning, the Pod will be requeued to activeQ/backoffQ soon.\n\tError\n\t// Unschedulable is one of the failures, used when a plugin finds a pod unschedulable.\n\t// If it's returned from PreFilter or Filter, the scheduler might attempt to\n\t// run other postFilter plugins like preemption to get this pod scheduled.\n\t// Use UnschedulableAndUnresolvable to make the scheduler skipping other postFilter plugins.\n\t// The accompanying status message should explain why the pod is unschedulable.\n\t//\n\t// We regard the backoff as a penalty of wasting the scheduling cycle.\n\t// When the scheduling queue requeues Pods, which was rejected with Unschedulable in the last scheduling,\n\t// the Pod goes through backoff.\n\tUnschedulable\n\t// UnschedulableAndUnresolvable is used when a plugin finds a pod unschedulable and\n\t// other postFilter plugins like preemption would not change anything.\n\t// See the comment on PostFilter interface for more details about how PostFilter should handle this status.\n\t// Plugins should return Unschedulable if it is possible that the pod can get scheduled\n\t// after running other postFilter plugins.\n\t// The accompanying status message should explain why the pod is unschedulable.\n\t//\n\t// We regard the backoff as a penalty of wasting the scheduling cycle.\n\t// When the scheduling queue requeues Pods, which was rejected with UnschedulableAndUnresolvable in the last scheduling,\n\t// the Pod goes through backoff.\n\tUnschedulableAndUnresolvable\n\t// Wait is used when a Permit plugin finds a pod scheduling should wait.\n\tWait\n\t// Skip is used in the following scenarios:\n\t// - when a Bind plugin chooses to skip binding.\n\t// - when a PreFilter plugin returns Skip so that coupled Filter plugin/PreFilterExtensions() will be skipped.\n\t// - when a PreScore plugin returns Skip so that coupled Score plugin will be skipped.\n\tSkip\n\t// Pending means that the scheduling process is finished successfully,\n\t// but the plugin wants to stop the scheduling cycle/binding cycle here.\n\t//\n\t// For example, the DRA plugin sometimes needs to wait for the external device driver\n\t// to provision the resource for the Pod.\n\t// It's different from when to return Unschedulable/UnschedulableAndUnresolvable,\n\t// because in this case, the scheduler decides where the Pod can go successfully,\n\t// but we need to wait for the external component to do something based on that scheduling result.\n\t//\n\t// We regard the backoff as a penalty of wasting the scheduling cycle.\n\t// In the case of returning Pending, we cannot say the scheduling cycle is wasted\n\t// because the scheduling result is used to proceed the Pod's scheduling forward,\n\t// that particular scheduling cycle is failed though.\n\t// So, Pods rejected by such reasons don't need to suffer a penalty (backoff).\n\t// When the scheduling queue requeues Pods, which was rejected with Pending in the last scheduling,\n\t// the Pod goes to activeQ directly ignoring backoff.\n\tPending\n)\n\n// This list should be exactly the same as the codes iota defined above in the same order.\nvar codes = []string{\"Success\", \"Error\", \"Unschedulable\", \"UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\", \"Wait\", \"Skip\", \"Pending\"}\n\nfunc (c Code) String() string {\n\treturn codes[c]\n}\n\nconst (\n\t// MaxNodeScore is the maximum score a Score plugin is expected to return.\n\tMaxNodeScore int64 = 100\n\n\t// MinNodeScore is the minimum score a Score plugin is expected to return.\n\tMinNodeScore int64 = 0\n\n\t// MaxTotalScore is the maximum total score.\n\tMaxTotalScore int64 = math.MaxInt64\n)\n\n// PodsToActivateKey is a reserved state key for stashing pods.\n// If the stashed pods are present in unschedulablePods or backoffQ，they will be\n// activated (i.e., moved to activeQ) in two phases:\n// - end of a scheduling cycle if it succeeds (will be cleared from `PodsToActivate` if activated)\n// - end of a binding cycle if it succeeds\nvar PodsToActivateKey StateKey = \"kubernetes.io/pods-to-activate\"\n\n// PodsToActivate stores pods to be activated.\ntype PodsToActivate struct {\n\tsync.Mutex\n\t// Map is keyed with namespaced pod name, and valued with the pod.\n\tMap map[string]*v1.Pod\n}\n\n// Clone just returns the same state.\nfunc (s *PodsToActivate) Clone() StateData {\n\treturn s\n}\n\n// NewPodsToActivate instantiates a PodsToActivate object.\nfunc NewPodsToActivate() *PodsToActivate {\n\treturn &PodsToActivate{Map: make(map[string]*v1.Pod)}\n}\n\n// Status indicates the result of running a plugin. It consists of a code, a\n// message, (optionally) an error, and a plugin name it fails by.\n// When the status code is not Success, the reasons should explain why.\n// And, when code is Success, all the other fields should be empty.\n// NOTE: A nil Status is also considered as Success.\ntype Status struct {\n\tcode    Code\n\treasons []string\n\terr     error\n\t// plugin is an optional field that records the plugin name causes this status.\n\t// It's set by the framework when code is Unschedulable, UnschedulableAndUnresolvable or Pending.\n\tplugin string\n}\n\nfunc (s *Status) WithError(err error) *Status {\n\ts.err = err\n\treturn s\n}\n\n// Code returns code of the Status.\nfunc (s *Status) Code() Code {\n\tif s == nil {\n\t\treturn Success\n\t}\n\treturn s.code\n}\n\n//
